<div id="review_2194815288" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194815288" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194815288?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=what-is-this-mess">what-is-this-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194815288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer156721612991403484">Listen, I am acknowledging this is not the best book ever written. But I am also telling you that I liked reading it <i>a lot.</i> <b>
  <u>It is no-holds-barred entertainment with hints of substance underneath that I’m hoping continue to develop</u>
</b>.<br/><br/>Audrey Rose does autopsies. On cadavers. This is obviously not generally considered acceptable for societal women in 1888. She is kind of not the most street smart person ever and keeps doing things that are completely lacking in common sense. I do not respect or l</span>
  <span id="freeText156721612991403484" style="display:none">Listen, I am acknowledging this is not the best book ever written. But I am also telling you that I liked reading it <i>a lot.</i> <b>
  <u>It is no-holds-barred entertainment with hints of substance underneath that I’m hoping continue to develop</u>
</b>.<br /><br />Audrey Rose does autopsies. On cadavers. This is obviously not generally considered acceptable for societal women in 1888. She is kind of not the most street smart person ever and keeps doing things that are completely lacking in common sense. I do not respect or like this about her. However, I like her as a concept [and no one ever said I had to be consistent]. Despite doing Things That Anyone Could Tell You Are Not Smart, she’s an interesting character with well-done emotional arcs. <br /><br />Also, I shockingly like the character of Thomas Cresswell? I think I was expecting stock asshole YA hero, but that’s not what I got. He’s not trying to be an asshole, he’s just genuinely obtuse about other people’s human emotions and other people in general. Which I like because I on some level relate. I like that the love interest has that trait, which is something I think we as a society usually frame as making a person terrible.<br /><br />In terms of the feminism I was kind of… no. Full disclosure, I do think this narrative will improve in further books. But the thing is, <b>
  <u>this book is not really that feminist.</u>
</b> I honestly think my favorite <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023671172?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a>, who <i>also</i> has read this book and <i>also</i> really likes Thomas Cresswell, put it best [as usual] - this book was <i>so</i> caught up in showcasing Audrey going against societal rules that it <b>
  <u>completely ignored and overshadowed other women in the narrative, and it is a lazy decision.</u>
</b> And as she also pointed out, <b>
  <u>Audrey’s Indian heritage is basically glossed over.</u>
</b> I have <i>two</i> original thoughts. My first original thought is that this book could have discussed colonialism way more if it were willing to make Audrey Rose’s dad a more nuanced character. [This is a really boring thought that everyone has already had]. Love that the heroine is half-Indian, but like… it is the 1880s in Britain and India is being brutalized right now. That would have been nice to mention once or twice, my guy. My second thought is that Thomas Cresswell should definitely have been a girl. Because the thing about this novel is it contains approximately four main characters aside from Audrey Rose, and all of them - by nature of the narrative and what it’s saying about male privilege - need to be men. Except for Thomas. And a book about two girls kicking ass and saving London together is sort of obviously more feminist than a book about one girl and one guy. Yes, I’m saying this book would be better if it were gayer, and yes, I’m right. Thanks.<br /><br />And now we get to the topic of the killer review, which you should not read about because going in without knowledge is always good! Okay, the funny thing is that enough people said the killer was obvious “from chapter two” that I was really expecting it to be even <i>more</i> obvious than it was, and I ended up thinking it was the <i>most</i> obvious candidate instead of the actual killer for like half the book, until I finally realized that was just way too obvious. So yeah, fine, <b>the reveal is kind of easy to guess.</b> But… I still like this killer reveal. This killer reveal is good because it doesn’t really depend on shocking you? I had heavily considered the possibility and it still just made me <i>sad</i> for Audrey Rose. Which I think makes for an overall stronger reveal.<br /><br />Anyway, I think this review is probably over because I’m tired of writing it. But I thought this book was <b>
  <u>really entertaining.</u>
</b> I haven't read book two yet - that might be the source of my decision on whether to recommend this - but I mean, I did enjoy it. Guiltily. So you might too.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_1707839892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1707839892" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1707839892?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=bad-romance">bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1707839892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10859986651065130108"><strong>Well that was a charming ending to a rather dark story. </strong><br/><br/>By that I mean the last three pages warmed my heart while the previous three hundred chilled my bones.<br/><br/><em>Stalking Jack the Ripper </em>was easily my most anticipated release of the second half of 2016. I wouldn’t go as far as to say that I’m fascinated by the horrifying personage that was Jack the Ripper, but my curiosity (and disgust) cannot help but awake at the mention of him and his doings.<br/><br/>Kerri Maniscalco created very ‘‘human’’ characters in t</span>
  <span id="freeText10859986651065130108" style="display:none"><strong>Well that was a charming ending to a rather dark story. </strong><br /><br />By that I mean the last three pages warmed my heart while the previous three hundred chilled my bones.<br /><br /><em>Stalking Jack the Ripper </em>was easily my most anticipated release of the second half of 2016. I wouldn’t go as far as to say that I’m fascinated by the horrifying personage that was Jack the Ripper, but my curiosity (and disgust) cannot help but awake at the mention of him and his doings.<br /><br />Kerri Maniscalco created very ‘‘human’’ characters in this story. Humans are, and we know this, highly flawed. We like them – we like our peers – but there are moments when we want to send them straight to hell.<br /><br />Audrey Rose, the heroine, as well as every single person surrounding her are strangely likeable despite all their flaws. As soon as I finished the first chapter, I was certain I would come to despise Audrey’s uncle to the core of my being… but he proved himself to be surprisingly endearing, as introverted and grumpy as he may be.<br /><br />Therefore, the characters are not ones I had any problem with. Truly, I cannot wait to see them again (the ones still alive that is, heheh) in the sequels.<br /><br />The writing style is another wonderful element of this book. Even when the story slowed down (very, very intensely), I still managed to enjoy myself with Maniscalco’s witty words. She captured the right atmosphere a mystery novel with dark scenes should have.<br /><br />Now, what I wished were different is the romance. Both Audrey and Thomas are intriguing and loveable so, individually, they are not a problem. But <em>together, </em>they are awkward and seem to exasperate each other to no end instead of awakening romantic feelings inside one another. What could have been an exciting case of ‘‘love-hate relationship’’ fell short.<br /><br />Furthermore, while the story is, overall, complex and well-written, it is not always <em>interesting</em> per se. Firstly, it’s quite slow and descriptive – so much I sometimes had to go back and reread dialogs to remember what the talking was about. And, secondly, the ‘‘stalking’’ Audrey and Thomas do, for the most part, helps little in the end, and reveals to be more reckless than courageous. And it’s not exactly ‘‘stalking’’ either, so you know.<br /><br />But, all in all, I don’t regret reading this book, for I had the chance to meet memorable characters and discover a new author with talent in weaving words. Not a book I will reread in the next ten years, but one I will certainly remember.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10859986651065130108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2080076568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2080076568" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2080076568?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2080076568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18342611327083472237"><b>**3.5-stars rounded up**</b><br/><br/><i>Stalking Jack the Ripper</i> is the first installment of the series of the same name, featuring our intrepid protagonist, Audrey Rose Wadsworth and her charming friend, Thomas Cresswell. <br/><br/>From the start, I was drawn to Audrey Rose. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595446474ra/29854178.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>She is really a great character, although at times, I'll admit, a little flat.<br/><br/>The idea behind her is really one I can get behind, however. A young lady who doesn't buckle under the pressures of conventional society. We stan.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547061095ra/26892926.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Audrey Rose wants to use </span>
  <span id="freeText18342611327083472237" style="display:none"><b>**3.5-stars rounded up**</b><br><br><i>Stalking Jack the Ripper</i> is the first installment of the series of the same name, featuring our intrepid protagonist, Audrey Rose Wadsworth and her charming friend, Thomas Cresswell. <br><br>From the start, I was drawn to Audrey Rose. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595446474ra/29854178.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She is really a great character, although at times, I'll admit, a little flat.<br><br>The idea behind her is really one I can get behind, however. A young lady who doesn't buckle under the pressures of conventional society. We stan.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547061095ra/26892926.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Audrey Rose wants to use her mind and more specifically, she wants to use it to study forensic medicine and thusly, crime. <br><br>She apprentices with her Uncle, which they have to keep secret from her father and the rest of the world. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498905004ra/23171999.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Her Uncle teaches at a local college, as well as consults with the local law enforcement on violent crimes. <br><br>When the Jack the Ripper killings begin, the bodies are brought to his laboratory to be examined. Due to that, Audrey Rose becomes interested and tangentially involved with the case. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1569515348ra/28205477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is during this early stage of the investigation that she first meets Thomas and a sort of hate-to-love relationship begins. <br><br>This is one of my favorite tropes, so I was absolutely down for that. The banter between them is really sweet and Thomas stole my heart right from the start.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540220389ra/26483932.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The setting is Victorian London, again, one of my favorites, but for me this didn't really feel that way. <br><br>I felt like it could have been set anywhere. The atmosphere wasn't as rich as I hoped it would be. Really, that's my only gripe with this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586667293ra/29278154.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, that and the fact that I felt certain sections dragged a bit or were slightly unnecessary.<br><br>Overall, I thought the mystery was fun and I did like the risky situations that Audrey Rose put herself in. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588463639ra/29400795.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I definitely plan to continue on with the series. In fact, the last page of this book probably bumped my star rating a half star. <br><br>I believe the next book features the legend of Dracula, so, totally my aesthetic!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540220389ra/26483933.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18342611327083472237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2987396564" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14336422355946060118">ive always had a morbid curiosity about serial killers. i find them absolutely fascinating and jack the ripper is one of the most notorious ones, so i knew right away this would be my cup of tea. <br/><br/>what i didnt expect to enjoy so thoroughly were the characters. i really appreciate what audrey roses character stands for - i love the idea of women making their own place in a society that dictates how to behave, what to wear, how to speak, etc. i really like that she always acts upon her curiosity, e</span>
  <span id="freeText14336422355946060118" style="display:none">ive always had a morbid curiosity about serial killers. i find them absolutely fascinating and jack the ripper is one of the most notorious ones, so i knew right away this would be my cup of tea. <br /><br />what i didnt expect to enjoy so thoroughly were the characters. i really appreciate what audrey roses character stands for - i love the idea of women making their own place in a society that dictates how to behave, what to wear, how to speak, etc. i really like that she always acts upon her curiosity, even when it is perceived as unladylike. <br /><br />but, i mean, if i had my own thomas cresswell, im pretty sure i would be doing all kinds of improper things just to be near him, too. amirite, ladies? he is giving off big ‘will herondale meets sherlock’ energy and my heart just cant take it. <br /><br /> athough the characters are great and the story is fun, it is very predictable. it kind of took away the enjoyment for me to a degree, so i wish it hadnt been so obvious, but the motive is new and original. especially since there has always been so much speculation about the jack the ripper. <br /><br />anyways, this was an entertaining read and i hope the series continues to be just as fun!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2425948242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425948242" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2425948242?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Helena by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/61504833-maica">✦ Maica ✦</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425948242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7578340635689877975"><blockquote>
<br/> <i>“Wield your assets like a blade, Cousin. No man has invented a corset for our brains. Let them think they rule the world. It’s a queen who sits on that throne. Never forget that. There’s no reason you can’t wear a simple frock to work, then don the finest gown and dance the night away. But only if it pleases you.”</i><br/>
</blockquote> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534194692ra/26123512.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Who else was legitimately obsessed with all <b>56</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40642-nancy-drew' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nancy Drew</a> novels, all <b>21</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/42018-the-famous-five' rel='nofollow noopener'>Famous Five</a> novels, and the <b>4 classic</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16135705-the-greatest-adventures-of-sherlock-homes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sherlock Holmes</a> novels growing up??? I had <i>binoculars, monoculars, mag</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7578340635689877975" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<br> <i>“Wield your assets like a blade, Cousin. No man has invented a corset for our brains. Let them think they rule the world. It’s a queen who sits on that throne. Never forget that. There’s no reason you can’t wear a simple frock to work, then don the finest gown and dance the night away. But only if it pleases you.”</i><br>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534194692ra/26123512.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Who else was legitimately obsessed with all <b>56</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40642-nancy-drew" rel="nofollow noopener">Nancy Drew</a> novels, all <b>21</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/42018-the-famous-five" rel="nofollow noopener">Famous Five</a> novels, and the <b>4 classic</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16135705-the-greatest-adventures-of-sherlock-homes" rel="nofollow noopener">Sherlock Holmes</a> novels growing up??? I had <i>binoculars, monoculars, magnifying glasses, listening devices, codebreaking books, fingerprinting kits</i>...the whole works! I literally thought that I’d be <b>a detective or a forensic investigator</b> in the future!!! (Then, I realised that I’m rubbish at sciences and there went that dream… xD) <br><br>My favourite course that I’ve ever taken was a <b>Forensics Science elective</b> in high school (and I’m currently a Master’s student at uni, so how sad is that, by the way?), where we learnt how to <i>investigate a crime scene, forensic anthropology, forensic odontology, blunt force trauma, blood spatter, ballistics, hair and fibres, fingerprints, arson, forgery, handwriting analysis, serial killers, presenting evidence in a courtroom</i>, and more! We even got to create our own crime scenes (leaving behind trace evidence to use as clues), whilst also having to solve the cases of our classmates! Needless to say, when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1861385386?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Maica</a> recommended this to me, I was <b>ecstatic</b>! <i>Thanks so much, lovely! &lt;3</i><br><br>Unfortunately, this buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483416058" rel="nofollow noopener">Saman</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874452097?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Bhavik</a> was only a <b>4-star rating</b> because, despite my enjoyment of the novel, for a mystery…I shouldn’t have <b>correctly guessed</b> the murderer by <i>CHAPTER FOUR</i>. I’m not going to spoil Jack the Ripper’s identity for you, but I found that the author’s choice for the serial killer came across as <i>lazy plotting</i>. It was too neat and easy. I would’ve liked something a bit more complex. A bunch of possible suspects with equally viable motives would’ve greatly improved this novel. As the novel progressed, the author also left <i>glaringly obvious</i> hints as to the killer’s identity, which was completely unnecessary. I would’ve preferred it to be more of a surprise. All great mysteries hinge on varying degrees of subtlety, something that this book certainly lacks.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534194692ra/26123513.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Having said that, there’s this Canadian crime drama telly series, named <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt2443340/" rel="nofollow noopener">Motive</a>, which I love. The gist of it is that every episode begins with the <b>revelation of both the victim and the killer</b>. The audience must piece together the evidence and clues throughout the episode along with the homicide detective, to make the connection between the victim and the killer, making this show a <b>“whydunit”</b>, rather than a typical <b>“whodunit”</b>. I approached this book from the same angle, once I figured out Jack’s identity. Since we were told the identities of the victims and the killer was fairly obvious, I spent the duration of the novel trying to <i>determine the motive</i> behind the killer’s actions. I highly recommend doing this, as well. It will definitely improve your enjoyment of this novel!!! Regardless, the <b>Sherlock Holmes deduction-game style of writing</b> was very entertaining! :D<br><blockquote>
<br> <i>“You simply need to hone your powers of deduction, Wadsworth. Look at the obvious and go from there. Most people ignore what’s right before their eyes. They believe they see, but oftentimes only view what they want.”</i><br>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534194692ra/26123514.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Audrey Rose Wadsworth</b> was an absolutely wonderful protagonist. She was a firm believer in <i>gender equality</i> and refused to conform to English society’s conventions in the 1880-era. Her sassy personality also resonates with us, living today in the 21st century. She’s not a doormat, who is satisfied in a meek position that’s subservient to a man. Rather than enjoying social teas like her peers, she preferred to spend her time studying forensic science in her Uncle’s laboratory. She was very kind and wished to bring justice to all of the murdered women that society had no care for, as they held unsavoury positions as prostitutes. If I had one complaint about her character, it would be the fact that her <i>internal feminist monologue</i> was awfully repetitive. The same thing was said over and over again in a variety of ways, which would grate on anyone’s nerves, no matter how much I agreed with it.<br><blockquote>
<br> <i>“I’d do everything in my power to solve this case for Miss Nichols. And for any other voiceless girl or woman society ignored.”</i><br>
</blockquote> <br>As Maica promised, I was completely enamoured by <b>Thomas Cresswell</b>!!! &lt;3 Sorry, Maica, but I’m stealing him away! MINE MINE MINE!!! :P Despite his boldness and arrogance, I also found him to be simultaneously witty and charming. I adored his entertaining banter with Audrey and how he loved to tease her. He was also incredibly sweet: <i>“'I went to several shops trying to find the exact scent...' He looked at his hands. 'I wanted to purchase it for you.'”</i> Their scenes together made me so happy and giddy! His detective skills were also fan-bloody-tastic as he channelled his inner-Sherlock Holmes, perhaps even putting Holmes to shame (not really, but it felt like it, at times). I have a feeling that he’ll make it onto my never-ending book-boyfriend list in no time!!! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534194692ra/26123515.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I <i>really loved</i> this book, which was an excellent début novel, and I can’t wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33784373.Hunting_Prince_Dracula__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___2_" title="Hunting Prince Dracula (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #2) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunting Prince Dracula</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30375937.Escaping_from_Houdini__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___3_" title="Escaping from Houdini (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #3) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Escaping from Houdini</a>. I highly recommend it to those who enjoy <b>historical romances</b> and <b>mystery novels</b>! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7578340635689877975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1778601501?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1778601501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16051951857261245200">3.5 Stars! I went very back and forth with this book. In the beginning, I absolutely adored the story but as it progressed, I frequently found myself loosing interest. Serial killers are a huge subject of fascination for me, so I was a little disappointed I didn't enjoy the story as much as everyone else. It's likely that my own expectations for the novel weren't fulfilled, which is why it wasn't a favorite. Despite all that, I did still enjoy it. It was fun and fairly entertaining. I think I ju</span>
  <span id="freeText16051951857261245200" style="display:none">3.5 Stars! I went very back and forth with this book. In the beginning, I absolutely adored the story but as it progressed, I frequently found myself loosing interest. Serial killers are a huge subject of fascination for me, so I was a little disappointed I didn't enjoy the story as much as everyone else. It's likely that my own expectations for the novel weren't fulfilled, which is why it wasn't a favorite. Despite all that, I did still enjoy it. It was fun and fairly entertaining. I think I just would have liked a more developed, in-depth story about investigating one of the most baffling unsolved murder cases in history.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2828110364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14285110891575369110">Oh boy. Please don't come after me, but y'all.... I did not play well with this one. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563126799ra/27827593.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm not going to hash out everything here, because I'm clearly in the minority, and also because you can read all of my similar thoughts on Jamieson's review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139230714?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a>. <br/><br/>To sum it up, the whodunnit was predictable from the first moment the villain was introduced on page, none of the interesting factors, such as Audrey's biracial heritage, were explored beyond inclusion for mere cosmetic detail, and DEAR GOD I WAS BORE</span>
  <span id="freeText14285110891575369110" style="display:none">Oh boy. Please don't come after me, but y'all.... I did not play well with this one. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563126799ra/27827593.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not going to hash out everything here, because I'm clearly in the minority, and also because you can read all of my similar thoughts on Jamieson's review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139230714?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>. <br><br>To sum it up, the whodunnit was predictable from the first moment the villain was introduced on page, none of the interesting factors, such as Audrey's biracial heritage, were explored beyond inclusion for mere cosmetic detail, and DEAR GOD I WAS BORED. I've heard so much about people adoring Thomas Cresswell, but he didn't feel any different than a carbon copy of the many book boyfriends that precede him in other series, minus the fact that he is thrown into the Victorian era rather than modern day. I hate that I didn't love this, but I also feel like it's best for me to stop with the series here, instead of forcing myself to continue on just because these books have worked so well for other readers. If you enjoy YA historical romance, this one may work well for you. </span>

<div id="review_3403386379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3403386379" />
    <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named"><img alt="She-who-must-not-be-named " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602257813p2/106473614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3403386379?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="user" itemprop="url" name="She-who-must-not-be-named " href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named">She-who-must-not-be-named </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to She-who-must-not-be-named  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/53964123-sam">sam</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3403386379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4697265395525930007"><b> <i>“What is a man's soul made of that a woman's is not?” </i></b><br/>The story features a strong and courageous female protagonist, <b>Audrey Rose </b>whose interest in autopsies overpowers her fear of ostracisation in the society and of her over-protective father. During the period when other girls of her age were courted by suitors, Audrey spent most of her time at her Uncle's, unearthing the mysteries of a diabolical serial killer <b> Jack The Ripper </b>, indulging in the acts of human dissection and witnessing sick ba</span>
  <span id="freeText4697265395525930007" style="display:none"><b> <i>“What is a man's soul made of that a woman's is not?” </i></b><br />The story features a strong and courageous female protagonist, <b>Audrey Rose </b>whose interest in autopsies overpowers her fear of ostracisation in the society and of her over-protective father. During the period when other girls of her age were courted by suitors, Audrey spent most of her time at her Uncle's, unearthing the mysteries of a diabolical serial killer <b> Jack The Ripper </b>, indulging in the acts of human dissection and witnessing sick barbarity inflicted by him on his victims.<br /><br />The story was everything it promised to be and more. <i>Audrey's </i>desire to be something more than what the society expected of her was laudable. She is driven by her need to prove herself worthy of her Uncle's teachings. But then, she also is driven by her desire to prove her worth to her Uncle's apprentice, the very handsome and charming <b> Thomas Creswell </b>.<br />When she first meets <i>Thomas</i>, instant sparks fly and we realise that there is more to their connection than just their common interest over the dead. When the plot twists don't please you, their conversations definitely will, or at least, <i>Thomas </i>will. <br /><br />The best part about the book is it stays true to its storyline, without lingering much on the romantic aspects. Although constant flirtations and teasings weave in and out throughout their investigation, they treat each other like equals, discussing their theories, ideas and drawing conclusions. One moment, <i>Thomas</i> is super charming in his own roundabout way and the other moment, he's serious about the investigation, almost without emotions, dissecting human bodies and scrutinising their psyche. Their romance unfolds slowly and smoothly, making us gorge the decadence of those tiny moments.<br /><br />The only reason I'm not giving it five stars is because the main plot twist (the identity of <i> Jack The Ripper</i>) was predictable. Nonetheless, minor plot twists are dropped here and there in the story. <br /><br />All in all, I loved the plot, <i> Thomas Creswell </i> and the narration, and I rate this book <b> 3.5 </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4697265395525930007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1894603850" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894603850" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894603850?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-couples">favorite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=best-audiobooks">best-audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=steampunk-ish">steampunk-ish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894603850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15879324745735552149">Full review update!<br/><br/>Wow okay this was super fun. I mean really - if you're in the market for YA Sherlock Holmes with a badass heroine and a super snarky (and charming) sidekick, definitely pick this up. I do have some mixed feelings about parts and I'll admit I skipped some chunks because ew, not for me. Some of the ending really rubbed me the wrong way, but you can see those details below in the spoiler tag.<br/><br/>Aubrey Rose is basically an unconventional female in her society. She's super into educat</span>
  <span id="freeText15879324745735552149" style="display:none">Full review update!<br /><br />Wow okay this was super fun. I mean really - if you're in the market for YA Sherlock Holmes with a badass heroine and a super snarky (and charming) sidekick, definitely pick this up. I do have some mixed feelings about parts and I'll admit I skipped some chunks because ew, not for me. Some of the ending really rubbed me the wrong way, but you can see those details below in the spoiler tag.<br /><br />Aubrey Rose is basically an unconventional female in her society. She's super into education and volunteers her time at her uncle's lab studying forensic science. And we get all the gory details, lol. So if you're here for that kinda thing, you'll enjoy it. If not, just skip over it. I'd say the story is just as enjoyable without the details of the... dead. <br /><br />And then she meets the cocky, ever so flirty Thomas Cresswell who is pretty much Captain Carswell Thorne from the Lunar Chronicles reincarnate. Ohmigosh he is pretty much the reason I loved this book. The banter and everythinggggggg yessss give me more.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Thomas smiled at my eye roll, puffing his chest up and standing with one foot proudly resting on a chair as if posing for a portrait. “I don’t blame you, I am rather attractive. The tall, dark hero of your dreams, swooping in to save you with my vast intellect. You should accept my hand at once.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Anyway, a string of murders starts going down and as the story progresses, Aubrey starts to realize the murderer might be connected to her family somehow. And of course, Thomas is there to annoy Aubrey while she figures it all out.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If I don’t murder you this afternoon, it’ll be a gift sent directly from God Himself, and I vow to attend services again,” I said, holding a hand against my heart.<br />“I knew I’d get you to church eventually.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I would just like to say, for the record (and friends can vouch for me...) I KNEW WHO THE MURDER WAS ALL ALONG. So I win a cookie or something, right? I KNEW IT I KNEW IT I KNEW IT.<br /><br />Anyway, I definitely was not into the saence part and I skipped it. Spirits are just not my thing, yo. I don't feel like I missed out on much.<br /><br /><b>***Minor spoilers below - don't read if you want to keep the mystery alive!***</b><br />(I'll hide the big ones in the spoiler tag)<br /><br />As far as the ending, I definitely felt a bit of glee knowing I guessed the killer, but aside from that, it was just really sad. I actually even teared up a bit. And honestly, some of it really rubbed me the wrong way. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like how they were going to help her brother escape after all that? I mean come on.. I get that it is super gut wrenching to find that out and I can't even imagine... but that does not mean he gets a get out of jail free card. And I was super uneasy about the suicide thing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But as far as the set up for the next book, I'm super on board with that. I'm already REALLY looking forward to it and trying to beg my way to an arc lol. Mostly I'm just hoping for lots of time with Thomas Cresswell, though I hope the banter stays alive!<br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15879324745735552149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1456627062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1456627062" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1456627062?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1456627062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6518587737808981307"><b>Well this was full of blood and bone and a spot o' tea, which is such a nice compilation.</b> Like shout out to the finale where Audrey Rose tries to calm everyone down and says "LET'S HAVE TEA AND THINK ABOUT THIS" wow I how she's literally the only sensible person in this book. However, I have to admit...I've basically read this entire story before lmao. It was in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24187925.These_Shallow_Graves' title='These Shallow Graves by Jennifer Donnelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>These Shallow Graves</a> and I <i>did</i> get bored in the middle of reading SJTR because I knew what was happening! I predicted the murderer like</span>
  <span id="freeText6518587737808981307" style="display:none"><b>Well this was full of blood and bone and a spot o' tea, which is such a nice compilation.</b> Like shout out to the finale where Audrey Rose tries to calm everyone down and says "LET'S HAVE TEA AND THINK ABOUT THIS" wow I how she's literally the only sensible person in this book. However, I have to admit...I've basically read this entire story before lmao. It was in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24187925.These_Shallow_Graves" title="These Shallow Graves by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">These Shallow Graves</a> and I <i>did</i> get bored in the middle of reading SJTR because I knew what was happening! I predicted the murderer like 100pgs in!! I JUST KNOW EVERYTHING I'M LIKE THE EYE OF SAURON.<br /><br />However it was still a downright good book and I want the next one immediately.<br /><br /><b>Also can we take a moment to shout out about how feminist this is?!</b><br />Obviously sexism is stampeding through the streets because it's 1800s and women are too delicate to do anything but crossstitch. So <i>that</i> was annoying to read, in the sense that I'm really tired of having my heroines have to prove themselves before they can have their plot. I'M JUST TIRED. Not saying it's not realistic though. Obviously. <i>Anyway</i> this was so so well done though?! Like <b>for one thing: Audrey Rose was like "why can't I cut up corpses AND dress prettily"</b> and heck I've never read that before?! Usually the girl is all shunning anything feminine to prove they are "tough" (WHICH IS SO POISONOUS: femininity never equals weakness) so the fact that this book praised BOTH was so freaking refreshing?!?<br /><br /><b>Also Thomas Cresswell was a gift.</b><br />He's an arrogant jackass but also uses that so he can flirt shamelessly with Audrey Rose <i>the whole freaking book</i> and not have anyone say "Oh wow, mate, look at all your feelings." Thomas has way too many feelings bless him ah hhahah.<br /><br /><b>So the plot? Predictable but I still loved the writing!</b><br />It actually took time to delve into the forensic side (WHICH IS AWESOME) and talk about how you can tell things about the death via looking at the bodies. Details = incredible. And the pacing was just downright good because it didn't drag us through useless scenes?! Every scene trotted the plot along at a good pace!<br /><br /><b>Although I DID think the ending was a bit easy.</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean just having Nathaniel (SO PREDICTABLE TO BE THE KILLER BTW) commit suicide so no one would have any moral dilemmas was a bit of "neat and tidy calm ending where no one gets too hurt". It could've been really interesting to explore how the family would've dealt with him and everything?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(Although I did just read the Large Print version and hOLY HECK it was also hardcover and I've lost feeling in all of my arms.)<br /><br /><b>OKAY SO FINNNNE EVERYONE. I GET WHY YOU LOVE IT SO MUCH!</b> I should've read it earlier. Happy?!? I will be finding the next ones directly haha and I'm excited to see where this goes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6518587737808981307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2276752821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2276752821" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2276752821?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2276752821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3741610855916199898"><i> “Pretend I am as capable as a man? <br/>Please, sir, do not value me so little!” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>Did you ever wonder what it would be like living at the time when Jack the Ripper was roaming the streets of London? <br/>And did you maybe think it would be awfully exciting to be part of the investigation? <br/>Well, then this is the perfect book for you. <br/>Audrey Rose was never the one for living under the rules of society. <br/>Women can’t be a medical apprentice? <br/>Women are only here to serve their husbands and be goo</span>
  <span id="freeText3741610855916199898" style="display:none"><i> “Pretend I am as capable as a man? <br />Please, sir, do not value me so little!” </i> <br /><br />Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Did you ever wonder what it would be like living at the time when Jack the Ripper was roaming the streets of London? <br />And did you maybe think it would be awfully exciting to be part of the investigation? <br />Well, then this is the perfect book for you. <br />Audrey Rose was never the one for living under the rules of society. <br />Women can’t be a medical apprentice? <br />Women are only here to serve their husbands and be good wifeys and go home? <br />That’s probably the stupidest thing ever. <br />That’s why Audrey Rose becomes an apprentice at her Uncles laboratory.<br />She partners up with the strange but really handsome Thomas Cresswell, who’s also an apprentice of her uncle. <br />Together they try to solve the murders by Jack the Ripper. <br />Even though I enjoyed the story, I wasn’t completely crazy about it. It was entertaining in some way, but I had the feeling it was kind of slow? Still I wanted to know who the killer was in the end, that’s why I continued reading it. <br /><br />Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Like I said I wasn’t the biggest fan of this book. It was enjoyable, but not like other books I’ve read.<br />But the characters... oh I really really liked them. <br />First of all Audrey Rose, the wonderful, strong and intelligent main character, who showed the man in this story that women are more than just beautiful objects. I loved her for the way she stayed her true self even though so many people tried to push her down. And she embraced her intelligence and the will to find the murderer. She didn’t think it was inappropriate to do so.<br />Also I loved her Indian background and the fact she was crazy about Indian foods/snacks. <br />That was the cutest. <br /><br /><i> “I’d like to remind each who held such poor opinions of a woman that their beloved mothers were, in fact, women. <br />I didn’t see any men running about, birthing the worlds population then going on to make supper and tend to the house. Most of them buckled to their knees when the slightest sniffle attacked them. </i> <br /><br />Then Thomas Cresswell, our handsome partner in crime. The best thing about him is definitely his intelligence. I mean, yes, he is sometimes inappropriate, but who cares? As long as he is that sweet, respectful and supportive partner, I take all his moodiness and weirdness.<br />Oh, and he kind of reminded me of Sherlock Holmes. But just a little bit. 😛<br /><br /><i> “I don’t blame you, I am rather attractive. The tall, dark hero of your dreams, swooping in to save you with my vast intellect. You should accept my hand at once.” </i> <br /><br />Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />If someone expected this to be a insta-love or even worse a love-on-first-sight then this is definitely not your type of book. <br />There’s subtle flirting between those two mixed with a little bit of hate, annoyance and suspicion.<br /><br />Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />English isn’t my mother language, so maybe that’s the reason why I didn’t fall in love with the writing of this book. It seemed really detail-filled and slowly even though I wanted some action. Still, I liked it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3741610855916199898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1681461349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1681461349" />
    <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader"><img alt="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579173421p2/43850323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1681461349?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader">Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=bored-me-to-death">bored-me-to-death</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=annoying-heroines">annoying-heroines</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1681461349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17792571631470750052"><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED</b><br/><br/><b>*this review fills with minor spoiler. Read at your own risk.*</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br/>"Roses have both petals and thorns, my dark<br/>flower. You needn't believe something weak because it appears deli-<br/>cate. Show the world your bravery."<br/></b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>Wow. I'm so freaking disappointed with this book. Look, I didn't even have high expectation toward the book, because I know my expectations toward books often don't end up well. So I might as well not to expect anything, but the things is, it's really hard not</span>
  <span id="freeText17792571631470750052" style="display:none"><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED</b><br><br><b>*this review fills with minor spoiler. Read at your own risk.*</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br>"Roses have both petals and thorns, my dark<br>flower. You needn't believe something weak because it appears deli-<br>cate. Show the world your bravery."<br></b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>Wow. I'm so freaking disappointed with this book. Look, I didn't even have high expectation toward the book, because I know my expectations toward books often don't end up well. So I might as well not to expect anything, but the things is, it's really hard not to expect anything when this book sounded so good and oh my God, the cover's so pretty! and yeah, I expected good things from this book. But the book didn't meet my not-so-high-expectation. <br><br>so here are the problems I have with this book. <br><br><u>
  <b>Audrey Rose Wadsworth</b>
</u><br><br>I could not feel any connection between me and her. <b>Like at all</b>. In my opinion, she was just so boring and flat character. Oh and she annoyed me too. Am I missing out something or is she just an annoying person? she felt responsible for something that wasn't her fault. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br>Somehow, some way, I was responsible for this man's death.<br></b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>So if I could talk to her directly I would say, " Are you kidding me? how can you responsible for that man's death? that is not your responsibility, Audrey Rose. That is the killer's responsibility. That's the killer's fault."<br>that also made me think, if I accidently fell from the staircase or slipped on the floor, would she feel responsible for not saving me or preventing it from happening? <br>I don't know whether I'm missing out something about this or she's just an annoying person. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487014719ra/21969114.gif" width="250" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The Romance</u>
</b><br><br>Honestly, I don't know what to say about about the romance besides boring and lack of the that romance spark. In my opinion, the romance was rushed and it made me think like " Wait ... what is happening?!?" when they were about to kiss. I'm not saying it's insta love, because in my opinion, it's certainly not an insta love, but the romance happened too fast and it was rushed. I think, I would like this book more, if the romance took longer or maybe no romance at all, because I could not feel the romance or the spark between them. The romance was like ... plain. Too fast. Boring. Meh. Bleh. Oh and the love interest was boring and I did not like him or felt any attraction toward him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521391290ra/25234337.gif" width="250" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>The Plot</b> <br><br>IT WAS PREDICTABLE. When I read books, most of the time my theories are wrong or I can't predict at all, But it's different with this book. I could find out who the killer was before even reaching 100 pages and when I read the ending, I was like " HAHAHAHAHAHA IT WAS SO PREDICTABLE. I KNEW IT ALL ALONG." <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499997888ra/23288086.gif" width="380" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Most of the time when I read the book, I was either bored or falling asleep. I swear, I had a hard time reading this book. The feeling I get when I read my textbook is mutual to the feeling I felt while reading it. <b>B O R E D.</b> and I laughed once while reading it and that's it. I didn't laugh anymore and the story bored me. I had no interest in reading it. Oh and I skimmed reading this book, because I just didn't want to spend more days to read it. I'd rather read something else than reading it. But, I admit the ending was good. Honestly, it was even better than the whole story. Or maybe I felt this way because I was relieved that I finally finished reading it? <br><br>this book didn't work for me. it just wasn't for me, I guess. <br><br>-------------------------------------------<br><br><s>
  <b>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW. All I can say now is that I could predict the killer easily. 😑 </b>
</s><br>--------------------------------------------<br><s>
  <b>So, I've heard so many things about this book and mostly they're good things and I'm pretty curious about this book. I hope it's not a disappointing book! *cross fingers* </b>
</s></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1803849549?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=i-will-go-down-with-this-ship">i-will-go-down-with-this-ship</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=kickass-heroine">kickass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=perfection">perfection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803849549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18247354885326029802"><i> Recommended to me by this poo, ♡<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/60915716' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ninjaflower</a> ♡ and recommended to her (and me) by the lovely, ♡ <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58260626-johanna' rel='nofollow noopener'>Johanna</a> ♡ <br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Happy now, guys??!  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </i><br/><br/>I felt like this book came out of nowhere and took everyone by surprise, I’m truly astonished. <br/><br/><i> Stalking Jack the Ripper </i> is narrated by Audrey Rose, a seventeen-year old girl who comes from an affluent family during the late 1880’s. Despite the expectations suited for her by society and her father, Audrey Rose defies their regulations by s</span>
  <span id="freeText18247354885326029802" style="display:none"><i> Recommended to me by this poo, ♡<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/60915716" rel="nofollow noopener">Ninjaflower</a> ♡ and recommended to her (and me) by the lovely, ♡ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58260626-johanna" rel="nofollow noopener">Johanna</a> ♡ <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Happy now, guys??!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </i><br /><br />I felt like this book came out of nowhere and took everyone by surprise, I’m truly astonished. <br /><br /><i> Stalking Jack the Ripper </i> is narrated by Audrey Rose, a seventeen-year old girl who comes from an affluent family during the late 1880’s. Despite the expectations suited for her by society and her father, Audrey Rose defies their regulations by sneaking away to her uncle’s laboratory to study forensic medicine. When an investigation breaks out concerning Jack the Ripper, Audrey Rose gets onto it and finds out that the theories she’s deducing are a <i> little </i> too close for comfort. <br /><br />I entered this book with no background knowledge whatsoever (well kinda – for the most part, okay!) and I have to say that I am utterly impressed at the turnout. <br /><br />The book is mysterious, charming (I’m looking at you Thomas), and especially witty. I absolutely adored the fact that the mystery was perplexing. As the reader tries to piece together the evidence to uncover the fiend, they begin to notice that there are <i> too </i> many characters who fit the description. <br /><br />Audrey Rose is a delight of a main character. She’s witty, intelligent, feminine, and fierce (especially when faced with all those gruesome images on a daily basis). <br /><br />Thomas Cresswell is the absolute perfect companion for our heroine. He’s absolutely hilarious, riling up Audrey in the most charming of ways. They are really fricken adorable together. <i> I sense a new ship emerging . . .</i> <br /><br />I <i> loved </i> the historic-ness of this book. It just made it all the more fascinating and enjoyable for me. <br /><br />So, and I say this with a sigh, I unfortunately did not solve the mystery before it was revealed. Sure, I had my doubts (and I did the whole, <i> do not trust anyone, </i> which is probably the best way to go about it) about each character but I just couldn’t piece together that <i> last </i> bit. <br /><br />But damn, was it awesome to try and figure out the culprit along the way. I thoroughly enjoyed this book and I <i> cannot </i> wait for the next book to be releases. *heart eyes*<br /><br /><i> “Roses have both petals and thorns, my dark flower. You needn’t believe something weak because it appears delicate. Show the world your bravery.” </i><br /><br /><br />5 stars!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18247354885326029802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2139230714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139230714" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
