        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2139230714?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series-to-complete">series-to-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=overhyped">overhyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2139230714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18148351344535046825"><i>
  <blockquote>"Roses have both petals and thorns, my dark flower. You needn’t believe something weak because it appears delicate. Show the world your bravery.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>yeah so ,, this was incredibly disappointing for me and everyone should just go watch the <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qg2nGY1aqlg' rel='nofollow noopener'>buzzfeed unsolved episode</a> instead</b> BECAUSE SHANE AND RYAN NEVER LET ME DOWN LIKE THIS BOOK DID. <br/><br/><i>this book has so many issues</i> all of which we will be going into later but the thing is, I probably could have overlooked them to some degree if this book was at least</span>
  <span id="freeText18148351344535046825" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"Roses have both petals and thorns, my dark flower. You needn’t believe something weak because it appears delicate. Show the world your bravery.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>yeah so ,, this was incredibly disappointing for me and everyone should just go watch the <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qg2nGY1aqlg" rel="nofollow noopener">buzzfeed unsolved episode</a> instead</b> BECAUSE SHANE AND RYAN NEVER LET ME DOWN LIKE THIS BOOK DID. <br /><br /><i>this book has so many issues</i> all of which we will be going into later but the thing is, I probably could have overlooked them to some degree if this book was at least entertaining but <u>despite this book a murder mystery and based on true crime it was so, so boring</u><br /><br />I definitely expected this book to have more direction. We're introduced to Audrey - a girl interested in science and crime. When murders start happening in her area she's compelled to investigate. I was expecting a pointed, driven book as Audrey raced to solve the crime but <b>honestly this book was a romance in which Audrey randomly stumbled upon clues</b> and considering Audrey was supposed to be bright and bold she was .. kind of dumb. I mean literally everyone I've seen review this book said they guessed who the murderer was on chapter 2, and so did I. <br /><br />On top of that, she just puts herself into ridiculous, silly situations. Like wandering off alone at night when there's a murderer, or stalking people into dark alleys, and I just was like GIRL I thought you were smart. <br /><br />And this all leads me to talking about Audrey Rose as a character because going into this I wanted to love her. But the whole time reading it I just wanted her to shut the hell up. <b>her monologues about feminism were hollow and irritating</b> and listen, I'm all for feminist characters, but WHY OH WHY are you trying to play off a girl who <u>complains about girls at literally every oppurtunity</u> as a feminist. Audrey Rose IS the "I'm not like other girls" girl and, seriously, you're not gonna sell that girls feminism to me.<br /><br />But we're gonna get back to feminism in this book in a minute too. <b>Lets talk about romance</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"There’s nothing better than a little danger dashed with some romance." </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The romance absolutely did not do it for me in this book. Is it just me, or is anyone else getting sooo bored of a book throwing a male and female character in the same room, and you can practically hear the author throwing their hands up in the air and saying "he was a boy, she was a girl, can I make it anymore obvious?"<br /><br />Because it was <b>so so obvious</b> what was gonna happen between Thomas and Audrey and I was never rooting for it. I need authors to start building up chemistry and genuine romance instead of relying on the fact and he's a guy she's a girl. <br /><br />On top of that, I did NOT like Thomas Cresswell at all. He's the sterotypical kind of rude, kind of obtuse but he's actually a softie deep down trope. And listen, if you like that you'll probably like him. Because he's not really a bad guy, but he just <u>exhausted me</u> and this book never compelled me to care about him or Audrey. Which is a BIG BIG problem when so much of this book is preoccupied with putting it's leads in romantic sleuthing situations. <br /><br />I basically know the romance isn't going well for me when I roll my eyes at the "I love you" moment and thats what happened here. <br /><br /><b>FEMINISM AND SIMILAR ISSUES</b><br /><br />The feminism was the whitest, fakest feminism ever. If you're going to write a book about feminism <b>then you should primarily be portraying women</b> is this not a no brainer? But throughout this whole book the only prominent female character is Audrey, and any other woman who appears is shunned by Audrey and ridiculed for not being "enlightened". I hated it so so much.<br /><br />Audrey is also biracial, her mum being Indian, but this fact is only used to talk about how Audrey has lovely skin and then completely glossed over for the rest of the book. Which is ,, weird. Especially in this time period. <b>the fact Audrey's rich, well off father was married to an Indian woman at a time when India was actively colonised by Britain would have been .. a bit of a deal</b> And while I'm all for not making people suffer for their marginalisations in historical fiction <u>if you're writing a book about how misogyny harms women in the 1800's, I feel like there's room for a realistic exploration of how race and racism plays into that too</u>. it just felt weird, fake, and definitely thrown in. <a href="http://blacksheepbsreviews.blogspot.com.au/2017/02/false-feminism-on-stalking-jack-ripper.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review nails my anger about the feminism</a><br /><br />I mean, Jack the Ripper was a man who, specifically, preyed on women (prostitutes particularly) which has some nasty implications about women, sexism and female sexuality. And when you look at the actual top suspects for Jack the Ripper <b>most of their motives are driven by gender dynamics</b> which means this book had an interesting oppurtunity to explore that and it DIDN'T. I was hoping for the Jane the Ripper version of events in this book to be honest. <br /><br />The mental illness representation was also a <b>straight up mess</b> I mean, we're shown a character who's supposedly mental ill, locked in an actual asylum, given some medicine and apparently is now completely cured ?? excuse me what :?? <br /><br />On a smaller note: The dialogue definitely annoyed me and some things were obviously not researched properly which was annoying. <br /><br /><b>THINGS I ACTUALLY LIKED</b><br /><br />Probably the only good thing about this book was the villain and their motives. While I guessed the killer early, their motives were interesting and original. And I thought the reveal was done fairly well, even though, again, it was obvious. I can see this was supposed to be more about the emotional impact and if I didn't know the villain was the villain I probably would have felt sorry for them. <br /><br />Also, I'm literally always here for steampunk elements and this book had some.<br /><i>
  <blockquote>Fear is a hungry beast. The more you feed it, the more it grows.<br /></blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I mean, <b>maybe if I wasn't excruciatingly bored through this book it would have been better</b> But due to the fact I was bored I then had to analyse literally every single flaw of this book to pass the time and I just urgh. <br /><br />If this book had nailed even ONE of it's elements I would have liked it so much more. But a book that's boring, portrays shoddy feminism and representation, coupled with a romance I didn't care about and an obvious plot twist it was just, not for me AT ALL. And I'm not going to continue this series probably.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18148351344535046825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J6kCTcX6TzTX2FHjyX5GSsYbGWugZrXjhqaxDmyMef3gaIRed9ZDXLOWEPVZ7/gqKDaRGgm1anj3I9dL1TDmlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1HTnGLObYyHKpnhwTawFziSklnaFJ/Wd3sKgNjKremoTtWELAbdvSa7oOWbdPbuuyokeByz0KgavR8ZzixflAg==')})
  }
//]]>
